					<h1 id="firstHeading" class="firstHeading mw-first-heading"><span class="mw-page-title-main">Blackfoot language</span></h1>

href="/wiki/Kainai_Nation" title="Kainai Nation">Kainai Nation</a> in southern <a href="/wiki/Alberta" title="Alberta">Alberta</a>; <a href="/wiki/Blackfeet_Nation" title="Blackfeet Nation">Blackfeet Nation</a> in <a href="/wiki/Montana" title="Montana">Montana</a></td></tr><tr><th scope="row" class="infobox-label" style="white-space:nowrap;padding-right:0.65em;">Ethnicity</th><td <ul style="line-height:100%; margin-left:1.35em;padding-left:0"><li>

</td></tr><tr><th scope="row" class="infobox-label" style="white-space:nowrap;padding-right:0.65em;"><div style="display: inline-block; line-height: 1.2em; padding: .1em 0;"><span class="wrap"><a <link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1066479718"><table class="infobox" style="background:#fff6d9"><tbody><tr><th scope="row" class="infobox-label" style="background:#fee8ab">People</th><td class="infobox-data"><a href="/wiki/Blackfoot_Confederacy" title="Blackfoot Confederacy">Niitsitapi (ᖹᐟᒧᐧᒣᑯ)</a></td></tr><tr><th scope="row" class="infobox-label" style="background:#fee8ab">Language</th><td class="infobox-data"><a class="mw-selflink selflink">Niitsipowahsin (ᖹᐨᓱᑲᖷᑊᓱᐡ)</a></td></tr><tr><th scope="row" class="infobox-label" style="background:#fee8ab">Country</th><td class="infobox-data">Nitawahsin'nanni (ᖹᒣᖷᑊᓱᐡ ᖻᐡᖹ)</td></tr></tbody></table> 
<p>The <b>Blackfoot language</b>, also called <b>Siksiká</b> (its denomination in <a href="/wiki/ISO_639-3" title="ISO 639-3">ISO 639-3</a>, <span class="rt-commentedText nowrap"><small>English:  </small><span class="IPA nopopups noexcerpt" lang="en-fonipa"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/English" title="Help:IPA/English">/<span style="border-bottom:1px dotted"><span title="/ˈ/: primary stress follows">ˈ</span><span title="&#39;s&#39; in &#39;sigh&#39;">s</span><span title="/ɪ/: &#39;i&#39; in &#39;kit&#39;">ɪ</span><span title="&#39;k&#39; in &#39;kind&#39;">k</span><span title="&#39;s&#39; in &#39;sigh&#39;">s</span><span title="/ə/: &#39;a&#39; in &#39;about&#39;">ə</span><span title="&#39;k&#39; in &#39;kind&#39;">k</span><span title="/ə/: &#39;a&#39; in &#39;about&#39;">ə</span></span>/</a></span></span> <a href="/wiki/Help:Pronunciation_respelling_key" title="Help:Pronunciation respelling key"><i title="English pronunciation respelling"><span style="font-size:90%">SIK</span>-sə-kə</i></a>; <small>Siksiká</small> <a href="/wiki/Help:IPA" title="Help:IPA">[sɪksiká]</a>, <small><a href="#Writing_system">syllabics</a></small> <span title="Blackfoot-language text"><span lang="bla">ᓱᖽᐧᖿ</span></span>), often anglicised as <i><b><span title="Blackfoot-language text"><i lang="bla">Siksika</i></span></b></i>, is an <a href="/wiki/Algonquian_languages" title="Algonquian languages">Algonquian</a> language spoken by the <a href="/wiki/Blackfoot_Confederacy" title="Blackfoot Confederacy">Blackfoot</a> or <span title="Blackfoot-language romanization"><i lang="bla-Latn">Niitsitapi</i></span> people, who currently live in the northwestern plains of <a href="/wiki/North_America" title="North America">North America</a>. There are four dialects, three of which are spoken in <a href="/wiki/Alberta" title="Alberta">Alberta</a>, Canada, and one of which is spoken in the United States: <span title="Blackfoot-language romanization"><i lang="bla-Latn">Siksiká</i></span> (Blackfoot), to the southeast of Calgary, Alberta; <span title="Blackfoot-language romanization"><i lang="bla-Latn">Kainai</i></span> (Blood, Many Chiefs), spoken in Alberta between Cardston and Lethbridge; <span title="Blackfoot-language romanization"><i lang="bla-Latn">Aapátohsipikani</i></span> (Northern Piegan), to the west of Fort MacLeod which is Brocket (Piikani) and <span title="Blackfoot-language romanization"><i lang="bla-Latn">Aamsskáápipikani</i></span> (Southern Piegan), in northwestern <a href="/wiki/Montana" title="Montana">Montana</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup> The name <i>Blackfoot</i> probably comes from the blackened soles of the leather shoes that the people wore.<sup id="cite_ref-Gibson_2003_3-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Gibson_2003-3">&#91;3&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<figure class="mw-default-size" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:2015_Siksika_Nation_Medical_Skills_Weekend.jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/00/2015_Siksika_Nation_Medical_Skills_Weekend.jpg/220px-2015_Siksika_Nation_Medical_Skills_Weekend.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="330" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/00/2015_Siksika_Nation_Medical_Skills_Weekend.jpg/330px-2015_Siksika_Nation_Medical_Skills_Weekend.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/00/2015_Siksika_Nation_Medical_Skills_Weekend.jpg/440px-2015_Siksika_Nation_Medical_Skills_Weekend.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3840" data-file-height="5760" /></a><figcaption>A sign at the Siksika Health and Wellness Centre in <a href="/wiki/Siksika_146" title="Siksika 146">Siksika 146</a> reads "<span title="Blackfoot-language text"><i lang="bla">Oki</i></span>", a Blackfoot greeting</figcaption></figure>
<p>There is a distinct difference between Old Blackfoot (also called High Blackfoot), the dialect spoken by many older speakers, and New Blackfoot (also called Modern Blackfoot), the dialect spoken by younger speakers.<sup id="cite_ref-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-4">&#91;4&#93;</a></sup> Among the <a href="/wiki/Algonquian_languages" title="Algonquian languages">Algonquian languages</a>, Blackfoot is relatively divergent in phonology and lexicon.<sup id="cite_ref-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-5">&#91;5&#93;</a></sup> The language has a fairly small phoneme inventory, consisting of 11 basic consonants and three basic vowels that have contrastive length counterparts. Blackfoot is a <a href="/wiki/Pitch_accent" class="mw-redirect" title="Pitch accent">pitch accent</a> language.<sup id="cite_ref-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-6">&#91;6&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Frantz_2017,_p._3_7-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Frantz_2017,_p._3-7">&#91;7&#93;</a></sup> Blackfoot language has been declining in the number of native speakers and is classified as either a threatened or endangered language.<sup id="cite_ref-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-8">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Like the other Algonquian languages, Blackfoot is considered to be a <a href="/wiki/Polysynthetic_language" title="Polysynthetic language">polysynthetic language</a> due to its large morpheme inventory and word internal complexity.<sup id="cite_ref-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-9">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup> A majority of Blackfoot morphemes have a one–to–one correspondence between form and meaning, a defining feature of <a href="/wiki/Agglutinative_language" title="Agglutinative language">agglutinative languages</a>. However, Blackfoot does display some <a href="/wiki/Fusional_language" title="Fusional language">fusional</a> characteristics as there are morphemes that are polysemous.<sup id="cite_ref-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-10">&#91;10&#93;</a></sup> Both noun and verb stems cannot be used bare but must be inflected.<sup id="cite_ref-11" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-11">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup> Due to its morphological complexity, Blackfoot has a flexible <a href="/wiki/Word_order" title="Word order">word order</a>.
</p><p>The Blackfoot language has experienced a substantial decrease in speakers since the 1960s and is classified as "severely endangered" by the UNESCO Atlas of the World's Languages in Danger.<sup id="cite_ref-12" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-12">&#91;12&#93;</a></sup> In Canada, this loss has been attributed largely to <a href="/wiki/Canadian_Indian_residential_school_system" title="Canadian Indian residential school system">residential schools</a>, where Indigenous students were often punished severely for speaking their first languages.<sup id="cite_ref-13" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-13">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup> Widespread language loss can also be attributed to the <a href="/wiki/Sixties_Scoop" title="Sixties Scoop">Sixties Scoop</a>, through which thousands of Indigenous children were taken from their families, often without parental consent, and relocated by the government into non-Indigenous families.<sup id="cite_ref-14" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-14">&#91;14&#93;</a></sup> As a result of these losses, the Blackfoot community has launched numerous language revitalization efforts, include the Piikani Traditional Knowledge Services and many more.
</p>
<meta property="mw:PageProp/toc" />
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Language_variations">Language variations</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Blackfoot_language&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Language variations"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p><b><big>Pied Noir</big></b>
</p><p><i>Pied-Noir</i> is an alternate name for the Blackfoot tribe. The exact translation is 'black foot' in French.<sup id="cite_ref-15" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-15">&#91;15&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p><b><small>Other</small></b> 
</p><p><span title="Blackfoot-language romanization"><i lang="bla-Latn">Siksikáíʼpowahsin</i></span><sup id="cite_ref-16" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-16">&#91;16&#93;</a></sup> (<small><a class="mw-selflink-fragment" href="#Writing_System">syllabics</a>:</small> ᓱᘁᓱᘁᖳᐟᑲᖷᑊᓱᐡ) and <span title="Blackfoot-language romanization"><i lang="bla-Latn">Niitsipowahsin</i></span><sup id="cite_ref-:3_17-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:3-17">&#91;17&#93;</a></sup> (ᖹᐨᓱᑲᖷᑊᓱᐡ) are two other language variations for Blackfoot.
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Classification">Classification</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Blackfoot_language&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Classification"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Blackfoot is a member of the Algonquian language family belonging to the <a href="/wiki/Plains_Algonquian_languages" title="Plains Algonquian languages">Plains</a> areal grouping along with <a href="/wiki/Arapaho_language" title="Arapaho language">Arapaho</a>, <a href="/wiki/Gros_Ventre_language" title="Gros Ventre language">Gros Ventre</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Cheyenne_language" title="Cheyenne language">Cheyenne</a>. Blackfoot is spoken in Northwestern Montana and throughout Alberta, Canada, making it geographically one of the westernmost Algonquian languages.
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Blackfoot_language&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: History"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>The Blackfoot people had been one of many Native American nations that inhabited the Great Plains west of the <a href="/wiki/Mississippi_River" title="Mississippi River">Mississippi River</a>. The people were <a href="/wiki/Bison_hunting" title="Bison hunting">bison hunters</a>, with settlements in what is now the northern United States and southern Canada. Forced to move because of wars with neighboring tribes, the Blackfoot people settled all around the plains area, eventually concentrating in what is now Montana and Alberta. Blackfoot hunters would track and hunt game, while the remaining people would gather food, and other necessities for the winter. The northern plains, where the Blackfoot settled, had incredibly harsh winters, and the flat land provided little escape from the winds. The Blackfoot Nation thrived, along with many other native groups, until the European settlers arrived in the late eighteenth century. The settlers brought with them horses and technology, but also disease and weapons. Diseases like smallpox, foreign to the natives, decimated the Blackfoot population in the mid-nineteenth century. Groups of Blackfoot people rebelled against the Europeans, such as <a href="/wiki/Mountain_Chief" title="Mountain Chief">Mountain Chief</a>'s tribe. But in 1870, a tribe of peaceful Blackfoot were mistaken for the rebellious tribe and hundreds were slaughtered. Over the next thirty years, settlers had eradicated the bison from the Great Plains. This took away the main element of Blackfoot life and the people’s ability to be self-sustaining. With their main food source gone, the Blackfoot were forced to rely on government support.<sup id="cite_ref-Gibson_2003_3-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Gibson_2003-3">&#91;3&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In 1886, the Old Sun Residential School opened on the <a href="/wiki/Siksika_146" title="Siksika 146">Blackfoot Reserve</a> in Alberta. In 1908, it was described by an official survey as "unsanitary" and "unsuitable in every way for such an institution". Regardless, it remained operational until its closure in 1971. Dozens of Blackfoot children died while attending.<sup id="cite_ref-18" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-18">&#91;18&#93;</a></sup> The school was rife with physical, sexual, and psychological abuse, which left a lasting impact on the Blackfoot children who attended.<sup id="cite_ref-19" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-19">&#91;19&#93;</a></sup> The trauma endured by students, as well as the subsequent repression of their Indigenous language and culture, has been credited, in part, with the loss in the number of Blackfoot speakers.<sup id="cite_ref-20" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-20">&#91;20&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Phonology">Phonology</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Blackfoot_language&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Phonology"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Consonants">Consonants</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Blackfoot_language&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Consonants"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Blackfoot has nineteen consonants, of which all but <span class="IPA nowrap" lang="und-Latn-fonipa" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/ʔ/</span>, <span class="IPA nowrap" lang="und-Latn-fonipa" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/x/</span>, <span class="IPA nowrap" lang="und-Latn-fonipa" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/j/</span> and <span class="IPA nowrap" lang="und-Latn-fonipa" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/w/</span> form pairs distinguished by length. One of the two affricates <span class="IPA nowrap" lang="und-Latn-fonipa" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/k͡s/</span> is unusual for being <a href="/wiki/Heterorganic" class="mw-redirect" title="Heterorganic">heterorganic</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-nlguide2_21-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-nlguide2-21">&#91;21&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-f1999_22-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-f1999-22">&#91;22&#93;</a></sup>
</p>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Vowels">Vowels</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Blackfoot_language&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Vowels"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Monophthongs">Monophthongs</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Blackfoot_language&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Monophthongs"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>Blackfoot has a vowel system with three <a href="/wiki/Monophthong" title="Monophthong">monophthongs</a>, <span class="IPA nowrap" lang="und-Latn-fonipa" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/i<span class="wrap"> </span>o<span class="wrap"> </span>a/</span>.<sup id="cite_ref-nlguide2_21-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-nlguide2-21">&#91;21&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-f1999_22-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-f1999-22">&#91;22&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-f2017_1_2_23-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-f2017_1_2-23">&#91;23&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<table class="wikitable" style="text-align:center">
<tbody><tr>
<th>
</th>
<th colspan="2"><a href="/wiki/Front_vowel" title="Front vowel">Front</a>
</th>
<th colspan="2"><a href="/wiki/Central_vowel" title="Central vowel">Central</a>
</th>
<th colspan="2"><a href="/wiki/Back_vowel" title="Back vowel">Back</a>
</th></tr>
<tr>
<th><a href="/wiki/Close_vowel" title="Close vowel">High</a>
</th>
<td style="border-right:0"><span class="IPA" lang="und-fonipa"><a href="/wiki/Close_front_unrounded_vowel" title="Close front unrounded vowel">i</a></span>
</td>
<td style="border-left:0"><span class="IPA nowrap" lang="und-Latn-fonipa" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">iː</span>
</td>
<td colspan="2">
</td>
<td style="border-right:0"><span class="IPA" lang="und-fonipa"><a href="/wiki/Close-mid_back_rounded_vowel" title="Close-mid back rounded vowel">o</a></span>
</td>
<td style="border-left:0"><span class="IPA nowrap" lang="und-Latn-fonipa" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">oː</span>
</td></tr>
<tr>
<th><a href="/wiki/Open_vowel" title="Open vowel">Low</a>
</th>
<td colspan="2">
</td>
<td style="border-right:0"><span class="IPA" lang="und-fonipa"><a href="/wiki/Open_front_unrounded_vowel" title="Open front unrounded vowel">a</a></span>
</td>
<td style="border-left:0"><span class="IPA nowrap" lang="und-Latn-fonipa" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">aː</span>
</td>
<td colspan="2">
</td></tr></tbody></table>
<p>The short <a href="/wiki/Monophthong" title="Monophthong">monophthongs</a> exhibit <a href="/wiki/Allophone" title="Allophone">allophonic</a> changes as well. The vowels <span class="IPA nowrap" lang="und-Latn-fonipa" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/a/</span> and <span class="IPA nowrap" lang="und-Latn-fonipa" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/o/</span> are raised to <span class="IPA nowrap" lang="und-Latn-fonipa" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">[ʌ]</span> and <span class="IPA nowrap" lang="und-Latn-fonipa" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">[ʊ]</span> respectively when followed by a long consonant. The vowel <span class="IPA nowrap" lang="und-Latn-fonipa" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/i/</span> becomes <span class="IPA nowrap" lang="und-Latn-fonipa" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">[ɪ]</span> in closed syllables.<sup id="cite_ref-f2017_1_2_23-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-f2017_1_2-23">&#91;23&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Diphthongs">Diphthongs</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Blackfoot_language&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Diphthongs"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>There are three additional <a href="/wiki/Diphthong" title="Diphthong">diphthongs</a> in Blackfoot. The first diphthong <i>ai</i> is pronounced <span class="IPA nowrap" lang="und-Latn-fonipa" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">[ɛ]</span> before a long consonant, <span class="IPA nowrap" lang="und-Latn-fonipa" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">[ei]</span> (or <span class="IPA nowrap" lang="und-Latn-fonipa" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">[ai]</span>, in the dialect of the Blackfoot Reserve) before <span class="IPA nowrap" lang="und-Latn-fonipa" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/i/</span> or <span class="IPA nowrap" lang="und-Latn-fonipa" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/ʔ/</span>, and elsewhere is pronounced <span class="IPA nowrap" lang="und-Latn-fonipa" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">[æ]</span> in the Blood Reserve dialect or <span class="IPA nowrap" lang="und-Latn-fonipa" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">[ei]</span> in the Blackfoot Reserve dialect. The second diphthong <i>ao</i> is pronounced <span class="IPA nowrap" lang="und-Latn-fonipa" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">[au]</span> before <span class="IPA nowrap" lang="und-Latn-fonipa" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/ʔ/</span> and <span class="IPA nowrap" lang="und-Latn-fonipa" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">[ɔ]</span> elsewhere. The third diphthong <i>oi</i> may be pronounced <span class="IPA nowrap" lang="und-Latn-fonipa" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">[y]</span> before a long consonant and as <span class="IPA nowrap" lang="und-Latn-fonipa" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">[oi]</span> elsewhere.<sup id="cite_ref-24" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-24">&#91;24&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Length">Length</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Blackfoot_language&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Length"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p><a href="/wiki/Vowel_length" title="Vowel length">Length</a> is contrastive in Blackfoot for both vowels and consonants. Vowel length refers to the duration of a vowel and not a change in quality. The vowel <span class="IPA nowrap" lang="und-Latn-fonipa" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/oo/</span> is therefore the same sound as <span class="IPA nowrap" lang="und-Latn-fonipa" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/o/</span> only differing in the length of time over which it is produced.<sup id="cite_ref-Frantz_2017,_p._3_7-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Frantz_2017,_p._3-7">&#91;7&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<dl><dd><table>
<tbody><tr>
<td><span title="Blackfoot-language romanization"><i lang="bla-Latn">áak<b>o</b>kaawa</i></span>
</td>
<td>
</td>
<td>
</td>
<td>'he will rope'
</td></tr>
<tr>
<td><span title="Blackfoot-language romanization"><i lang="bla-Latn">áak<b>oo</b>kaawa</i></span>
</td>
<td>
</td>
<td>
</td>
<td>'she will sponsor a Sundance'
</td></tr></tbody></table></dd></dl>
<p>Consonants can also be lengthened with the exception of  <span class="IPA nowrap" lang="und-Latn-fonipa" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/ʔ/</span>, <span class="IPA nowrap" lang="und-Latn-fonipa" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/x/</span>, <span class="IPA nowrap" lang="und-Latn-fonipa" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/j/</span> and <span class="IPA nowrap" lang="und-Latn-fonipa" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/w/</span>.
</p>
<dl><dd><table>
<tbody><tr>

</td>

<td>'one hundred'
</td></tr>
<tr>
<td><span title="Blackfoot-language romanization"><i lang="bla-Latn">ní<b>nn</b>a</i></span>

<td>'my father'
</td></tr>
<tr>
<td><span title="Blackfoot-language romanization"><i lang="bla-Latn">sokáʼp<b>ss</b>iwa</i></span>
</td>
<td>
</td>
<td>
</td>
<td>'he is good'
</td></tr></tbody></table></dd></dl>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Pitch_accent">Pitch accent</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Blackfoot_language&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Pitch accent"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Blackfoot is a <a href="/wiki/Pitch_accent" class="mw-redirect" title="Pitch accent">pitch accent</a> language and it is a contrastive feature in the language. Every word will have at least one high pitched vowel or diphthong but may have more than one. Note that high pitch here is used relative to the contiguous syllables. Blackfoot utterances experience a gradual drop in pitch therefore if an utterance contains a set of accented vowels the first will be higher in pitch than the second but the second will be higher in pitch than the syllables directly surrounding it. Pitch is illustrated in the Latin-based orthography with an acute accent.<sup id="cite_ref-Frantz_2017,_p._3_7-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Frantz_2017,_p._3-7">&#91;7&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<dl><dd><table>
<tbody><tr>
<td><span title="Blackfoot-language romanization"><i lang="bla-Latn">ápssiwa</i></span>
</td>
<td>
</td>
<td>
</td>
<td>'it's an arrow'
</td></tr>
<tr>
<td><span title="Blackfoot-language romanization"><i lang="bla-Latn">apssíwa</i></span>
</td>
<td>
</td>
<td>
</td>
<td>'it's a fig'
</td></tr>
<tr>
<td><span title="Blackfoot-language romanization"><i lang="bla-Latn">máátaissikópiiwa</i></span>
</td>
<td>
</td>
<td>
</td>
<td>'s/he's not resting'
</td></tr></tbody></table></dd></dl>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Phonological_rules">Phonological rules</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Blackfoot_language&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Phonological rules"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Blackfoot is rich with morpho-phonological changes. Below is a limited sample of phonological rules.
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Semi-vowel_loss">Semi-vowel loss</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Blackfoot_language&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Semi-vowel loss"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>Glides are deleted after another consonant, except a glottal stop, or word initially but kept in other conditions.<sup id="cite_ref-25" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-25">&#91;25&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<dl><dd><table>
<tbody><tr>
<td>
</td>

</td>
<td>
</td></tr>

<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Accent_spread">Accent spread</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Blackfoot_language&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Accent spread"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>Accent will spread from an accented vowel to the following vowel across morpheme boundaries.<sup id="cite_ref-26" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-26">&#91;26&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<dl><dd><table>

<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Vowel_devoicing">Vowel devoicing</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Blackfoot_language&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Vowel devoicing"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>At the end of a word, non-high pitched vowels are devoiced, regardless of length.<sup id="cite_ref-27" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-27">&#91;27&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span id="Grammar_.E2.80.93_general"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Grammar_–_general">Grammar – general</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Blackfoot_language&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Grammar – general"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Lexical_categories">Lexical categories</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Blackfoot_language&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Lexical categories"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Lexical categories in Blackfoot are a matter of debate in the literature, with the exception of nouns and verbs. Additional proposed categories, proposed by Uhlenbeck, are adjectives, pronouns, adverbs, and particles.<sup id="cite_ref-28" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-28">&#91;28&#93;</a></sup> Taylor classifies the Blackfoot language as having two major classes, substantives (nouns and pronouns) and verbs, with one minor class consisting of particles.<sup id="cite_ref-29" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-29">&#91;29&#93;</a></sup> Frantz classifies adjectives and adverbs as affixes but not independent classes.<sup id="cite_ref-30" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-30">&#91;30&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Agreement">Agreement</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Blackfoot_language&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Agreement"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Agreement morphology is extensive in Blackfoot and agreement morphemes are often <a href="/wiki/Fusional" class="mw-redirect" title="Fusional">fusional</a>, i.e. animacy and number (nouns) or person and number (verbs) are indicated within the same affix.
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Animacy">Animacy</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Blackfoot_language&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Animacy"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>All nouns are required to be inflected for <a href="/wiki/Animacy" title="Animacy">animacy</a> and are classified as either animate or inanimate. Verbs are inflected to match the animacy of its arguments. Animacy in Blackfoot is a grammatical construct for noun classification. Therefore, some semantically inherently inanimate objects, such as drums and knives are grammatically animate.<sup id="cite_ref-Frantz_2017,_p._7-10_31-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Frantz_2017,_p._7-10-31">&#91;31&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Verbs are marked with a transitivity marker which must agree with the animacy of its arguments. Even in stories in which grammatically inanimate objects are markedly anthropomorphized, such as talking flowers, speakers will not use animate agreement markers with them.
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Number">Number</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Blackfoot_language&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Number"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>All nouns are required to be inflected as either singular or plural. Verbal inflection matches the number of its arguments.<sup id="cite_ref-Frantz_2017,_p._7-10_31-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Frantz_2017,_p._7-10-31">&#91;31&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Person_marking">Person marking</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Blackfoot_language&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Person marking"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>Blackfoot has five grammatical persons&#160;– first, second, third (proximate), fourth (obviative), and fifth (sub-obviative).<sup id="cite_ref-32" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-32">&#91;32&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Word_order">Word order</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Blackfoot_language&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Word order"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p><a href="/wiki/Word_order" title="Word order">Word order</a> is flexible in Blackfoot. Subjects are not required to precede the verb.<sup id="cite_ref-33" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-33">&#91;33&#93;</a></sup> Independent noun phrases may be included but these are typically dropped in Blackfoot. Due to the extensive person inflection on the verb they are not necessary for interpreting the meaning of the utterance. However, if first or second person pronouns are present it yields an emphatic reading.<sup id="cite_ref-Frantz_2017,_p._22_34-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Frantz_2017,_p._22-34">&#91;34&#93;</a></sup> There is an ordering restriction if the Distinct Third Person (DTP) attached pronoun <span class="IPA nowrap" lang="bla-Latn-fonipa" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/-aawa/</span> is used in which the subject independent noun phrase must occur before the verb. If the independent noun phrase occurs after the verb then the DTP may not be used.<sup id="cite_ref-35" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-35">&#91;35&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Subjecthood">Subjecthood</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Blackfoot_language&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Subjecthood"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Blackfoot nouns must be grammatically particular in order to be a subject of a verb.<sup id="cite_ref-Frantz_2017,_p._22_34-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Frantz_2017,_p._22-34">&#91;34&#93;</a></sup> In transitive constructions the subject must be volitional to be interpreted as subject.<sup id="cite_ref-36" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-36">&#91;36&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Person_hierarchy">Person hierarchy</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Blackfoot_language&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Person hierarchy"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>It has been asserted that Blackfoot, along with other Algonquian languages, violates the Universal Person Hierarchy in verb complexes by ranking second person over first person. The hierarchy has traditionally been published as 2nd person &gt; 1st person &gt; 3rd person (proximate) &gt; 4th person (obviative).<sup id="cite_ref-37" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-37">&#91;37&#93;</a></sup> However, alternative analyses of Blackfoot person hierarchy have been published that suggest the Universal Person Hierarchy is applicable to Blackfoot.<sup id="cite_ref-38" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-38">&#91;38&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Verbal_structure">Verbal structure</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Blackfoot_language&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: Verbal structure"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The Blackfoot verbal template contains a stem with several prefixes and suffixes. The structure of the verb stem in Blackfoot can be roughly broken down into the pre-verb, the root, the medial, and the final. The root and final are required elements.
</p><p>Generally, information encoded in the pre-verb can include adverbs, most pronouns, locatives, manners, aspect, mood, and tense. Incorporated objects appear in the medial. The final includes transitivity and animacy markers, and valency markers.
</p>
<h2><span id="Grammar_.E2.80.93_nouns"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Grammar_–_nouns">Grammar – nouns</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Blackfoot_language&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: Grammar – nouns"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Agreement_morphology">Agreement morphology</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Blackfoot_language&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: Agreement morphology"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Noun classes are split based on <a href="/wiki/Grammatical_gender" title="Grammatical gender">grammatical gender</a> into two categories: animate and inanimate.<sup id="cite_ref-39" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-39">&#91;39&#93;</a></sup> Additionally, all nouns must be marked for number. Number agreement suffixes attach to noun stems and take four forms, as shown in the table below.<sup id="cite_ref-Frantz_2017,_p._7-10_31-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Frantz_2017,_p._7-10-31">&#91;31&#93;</a></sup>
</p>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Proximate_and_obviative">Proximate and obviative</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Blackfoot_language&amp;action=edit&amp;section=27" title="Edit section: Proximate and obviative"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>When a sentence contains two or more particular animate gender nouns as arguments proximate (major third person/3rd) and obviative (minor third person/4th) markings are used to disambiguate. There may only be one proximate argument in any given sentence but multiple obviates are permissible. Proximate arguments are more prominent in discourse. Redirectional markers, referred to as inverse and direct theme in the literature, can be applied to indicate that the fourth person is the subject argument.<sup id="cite_ref-40" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-40">&#91;40&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span id="Particularity.2Freferentiality"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Particularity/referentiality">Particularity/referentiality</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Blackfoot_language&amp;action=edit&amp;section=28" title="Edit section: Particularity/referentiality"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Blackfoot nouns must be grammatically particular, according to Frantz (2009), in order to be a subject of a verb. To be the subject of any verb in Blackfoot the noun must point to a specific referent in the world. In transitive constructions the subject must also be volitional to be interpreted as subject. If the subject of a transitive verb is non-specific or non-volitional then the verb must be inflected as having an unspecified subject.<sup id="cite_ref-41" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-41">&#91;41&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="interlinear" style="margin-left:3em"><div style="float: left; margin-bottom: 0.3em;margin-right: 1em;"><p lang="bla-latn" style="margin: 0px;font-style: italic;">Oma</p><p style="margin: 0px;">om-wa</p><p style="margin: 0px;">that-<abbr class="gloss-abbr" title="animate" style="font-variant: small-caps; font-variant-numeric: oldstyle-nums; text-transform: lowercase;">AN</abbr>.<abbr class="gloss-abbr" title="singular number" style="font-variant: small-caps; font-variant-numeric: oldstyle-nums; text-transform: lowercase;">SG</abbr></p></div><div style="float: left; margin-bottom: 0.3em;margin-right: 1em;"><p lang="bla-latn" style="margin: 0px;font-style: italic;">isttoána</p><p style="margin: 0px;">isttoan-wa</p><p style="margin: 0px;">knife-<abbr class="gloss-abbr" title="animate" style="font-variant: small-caps; font-variant-numeric: oldstyle-nums; text-transform: lowercase;">AN</abbr>.<abbr class="gloss-abbr" title="singular number" style="font-variant: small-caps; font-variant-numeric: oldstyle-nums; text-transform: lowercase;">SG</abbr></p></div><div style="float: left; margin-bottom: 0.3em;margin-right: 1em;"><p lang="bla-latn" style="margin: 0px;font-style: italic;">iihtsíkahksiniiʼpi</p><p style="margin: 0px;">iiht-íkahksinii-ʼp-yi</p><p style="margin: 0px;">means-cut.off-<abbr class="gloss-abbr" title="non-specific" style="font-variant: small-caps; font-variant-numeric: oldstyle-nums; text-transform: lowercase;">UNSPEC</abbr>.<abbr class="gloss-abbr" title="subject" style="font-variant: small-caps; font-variant-numeric: oldstyle-nums; text-transform: lowercase;">SUB</abbr>-<abbr class="gloss-abbr" title="inanimate gender" style="font-variant: small-caps; font-variant-numeric: oldstyle-nums; text-transform: lowercase;">INAN</abbr>.<abbr class="gloss-abbr" title="plural number" style="font-variant: small-caps; font-variant-numeric: oldstyle-nums; text-transform: lowercase;">PL</abbr></p></div><div style="float: left; margin-bottom: 0.3em;margin-right: 1em;"><p lang="bla-latn" style="margin: 0px;font-style: italic;">annistsi</p><p style="margin: 0px;">ann-istsi</p><p style="margin: 0px;">that-<abbr class="gloss-abbr" title="inanimate gender" style="font-variant: small-caps; font-variant-numeric: oldstyle-nums; text-transform: lowercase;">INAN</abbr>.<abbr class="gloss-abbr" title="plural number" style="font-variant: small-caps; font-variant-numeric: oldstyle-nums; text-transform: lowercase;">PL</abbr></p></div><div style="float: left; margin-bottom: 0.3em;margin-right: 1em;"><p lang="bla-latn" style="margin: 0px;font-style: italic;">ikkstsíksiistsi.</p><p style="margin: 0px;">ikkstsíksi-istsi</p><p style="margin: 0px;">branch-<abbr class="gloss-abbr" title="inanimate gender" style="font-variant: small-caps; font-variant-numeric: oldstyle-nums; text-transform: lowercase;">INAN</abbr>.<abbr class="gloss-abbr" title="plural number" style="font-variant: small-caps; font-variant-numeric: oldstyle-nums; text-transform: lowercase;">PL</abbr></p></div><p style="display: none;">Oma isttoána iihtsíkahksiniiʼpi annistsi ikkstsíksiistsi.</p><p style="display: none;">om-wa isttoan-wa iiht-íkahksinii-ʼp-yi ann-istsi ikkstsíksi-istsi</p><p style="display: none;">that-AN.SG knife-AN.SG means-cut.off-UNSPEC.SUB-INAN.PL that-INAN.PL branch-INAN.PL</p><p style="clear: left;">'The knife cut off those branches.' or 'By means of the knife, the branches were cut off.'</p><div style="clear: left; display: block;"></div>
</div>
<h2><span id="Grammar_.E2.80.93_verbs"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Grammar_–_verbs">Grammar – verbs</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Blackfoot_language&amp;action=edit&amp;section=29" title="Edit section: Grammar – verbs"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Verbal_morphology_template">Verbal morphology template</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Blackfoot_language&amp;action=edit&amp;section=30" title="Edit section: Verbal morphology template"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>There are four verb categories in Blackfoot: intransitive inanimate, intransitive animate, transitive inanimate, and transitive animate. The parameters of transitivity and animacy for verb selection are typically referred to as stem agreement in order to delineate it from person agreement. The animacy for intransitive verbs is determined by the subject of the verb whereas the transitive verbs are defined by the animacy of their primary object.<sup id="cite_ref-42" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-42">&#91;42&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The only required component of a clause in Blackfoot is the verb, referred to as a verbal complex in the Algonquian literature, that must be appropriately inflected according to the standard template:		 	
</p>
<blockquote><p>preverb – root – medial – final</p></blockquote>
<p>Preverbs are prefixes which encode adverbs, most pronouns, locatives, manners, aspect, mood, and tense. Medials are suffixes which primarily encode manner and incorporated objects. Finals are suffixes which encode transitivity, animacy, and valency. Roots and finals are always required in a verbal complex whereas preverb and medials are not.<sup id="cite_ref-43" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-43">&#91;43&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Inverse_and_direct_theme">Inverse and direct theme</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Blackfoot_language&amp;action=edit&amp;section=31" title="Edit section: Inverse and direct theme"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>When there are two animate arguments acting in a transitive animate verb stem one of the arguments must be acting on the other. Which argument is the actor (subject) and which is the acted upon (object) is indicated by the use of direct or inverse theme marking. If a subject argument is higher than the object argument on the person hierarchy then the direct suffix is used. Conversely, when an object outranks the sentences subject then the inverse suffix is used.<sup id="cite_ref-44" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-44">&#91;44&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<dl><dt>Direct</dt></dl>
<div class="interlinear" style="margin-left:3em"><div style="float: left; margin-bottom: 0.3em;margin-right: 1em;"><p lang="bla-latn" style="margin: 0px;font-style: italic;">Nitsikákomimmayi</p><p style="margin: 0px;">nit-ikákomimm-aa-yi</p><p style="margin: 0px;"><abbr class="gloss-abbr" title="first person" style="font-variant: small-caps; font-variant-numeric: oldstyle-nums; text-transform: lowercase;">1</abbr>.<abbr class="gloss-abbr" title="singular number" style="font-variant: small-caps; font-variant-numeric: oldstyle-nums; text-transform: lowercase;">SG</abbr>-love-<abbr class="gloss-abbr" title="directional" style="font-variant: small-caps; font-variant-numeric: oldstyle-nums; text-transform: lowercase;">DIR</abbr>-<abbr class="gloss-abbr" title="third person" style="font-variant: small-caps; font-variant-numeric: oldstyle-nums; text-transform: lowercase;">3</abbr>.<abbr class="gloss-abbr" title="plural number" style="font-variant: small-caps; font-variant-numeric: oldstyle-nums; text-transform: lowercase;">PL</abbr></p></div><div style="float: left; margin-bottom: 0.3em;margin-right: 1em;"><p lang="bla-latn" style="margin: 0px;font-style: italic;">nitániksi.</p><p style="margin: 0px;">ni-táni-iksi</p><p style="margin: 0px;"><abbr class="gloss-abbr" title="first person" style="font-variant: small-caps; font-variant-numeric: oldstyle-nums; text-transform: lowercase;">1</abbr>.<abbr class="gloss-abbr" title="possessive marker" style="font-variant: small-caps; font-variant-numeric: oldstyle-nums; text-transform: lowercase;">POSS</abbr>-daughter-<abbr class="gloss-abbr" title="animate" style="font-variant: small-caps; font-variant-numeric: oldstyle-nums; text-transform: lowercase;">AN</abbr>.<abbr class="gloss-abbr" title="plural number" style="font-variant: small-caps; font-variant-numeric: oldstyle-nums; text-transform: lowercase;">PL</abbr></p></div><p style="display: none;">Nitsikákomimmayi nitániksi.</p><p style="display: none;">nit-ikákomimm-aa-yi ni-táni-iksi</p><p style="display: none;">1.SG-love-DIR-3.PL 1.POSS-daughter-AN.PL</p><p style="clear: left;">'I love my daughters.'</p><div style="clear: left; display: block;"></div>
</div>
<dl><dt>Inverse</dt></dl>
<div class="interlinear" style="margin-left:3em"><div style="float: left; margin-bottom: 0.3em;margin-right: 1em;"><p lang="bla-latn" style="margin: 0px;font-style: italic;">Nitsikákomimmoki</p><p style="margin: 0px;">nit-ikákomimm-ok-yi</p><p style="margin: 0px;"><abbr class="gloss-abbr" title="first person" style="font-variant: small-caps; </div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Voice_and_valency">Voice and valency</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Blackfoot_language&amp;action=edit&amp;section=32" title="Edit section: Voice and valency"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Blackfoot voice alterations occur as suffixes on the verb and fall into the category of finals. Finals can include causative, benefactive, reciprocal, and reflexive affixes that either decrease or increase the valency of the stem they are attached to. Below is an example of the reflexive final suffix. It can only be added to a transitive animate stem and results in an animate intransitive stem. This is then interpreted as being a reflexive verb, where the subject of the AI (animate intransitive) stem is understood to be both the underlying subject and object of the original verb stem.<sup id="cite_ref-45" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-45">&#91;45&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="interlinear" style="margin-left:3em"><div style="float: left; margin-bottom: 0.3em;margin-right: 1em;"><p lang="bla-latn" style="margin: 0px;font-style: italic;">oma</p><p style="margin: 0px;">om-wa</p><p style="margin: 0px;">that-<abbr class="gloss-abbr" title="animate" style="font-variant: small-caps; font-variant-numeric: oldstyle-nums; text-transform: lowercase;">AN</abbr>.<abbr class="gloss-abbr" title="singular number" style="font-variant: small-caps; font-variant-numeric: oldstyle-nums; text-transform: lowercase;">SG</abbr></p></div><div style="float: left; margin-bottom: 0.3em;margin-right: 1em;"><p lang="bla-latn" style="margin: 0px;font-style: italic;">imitááwa</p><p style="margin: 0px;">imitáá-wa</p><p style="margin: 0px;">dog-<abbr class="gloss-abbr" title="animate" style="font-variant: small-caps; font-variant-numeric: oldstyle-nums; text-transform: lowercase;">AN</abbr>.<abbr class="gloss-abbr" title="singular number" style="font-variant: small-caps; font-variant-numeric: oldstyle-nums; text-transform: lowercase;">SG</abbr></p></div><div style="float: left; margin-bottom: 0.3em;margin-right: 1em;"><p lang="bla-latn" style="margin: 0px;font-style: italic;">siiksípohsiwa</p><p style="margin: 0px;">siiksip-o꞉hsi-wa</p><p style="margin: 0px;"><abbr class="gloss-abbr" title="past tense" style="font-variant: small-caps; font-variant-numeric: oldstyle-nums; text-transform: lowercase;">PST</abbr>:bite(<abbr class="gloss-abbr" title="transitive animate" style="font-variant: small-caps; font-variant-numeric: oldstyle-nums; text-transform: lowercase;">TA</abbr>)-<abbr class="gloss-abbr gloss-abbr-ambiguous" title="reflexive" style="font-variant: small-caps; font-variant-numeric: oldstyle-nums; text-transform: lowercase;">REFL</abbr>(<abbr class="gloss-abbr" title="animate intransitive" style="font-variant: small-caps; font-variant-numeric: oldstyle-nums; text-transform: lowercase;">AI</abbr>)-<abbr class="gloss-abbr" title="third person" style="font-variant: small-caps; font-variant-numeric: oldstyle-nums; text-transform: lowercase;">3</abbr>.<abbr class="gloss-abbr" title="singular number" style="font-variant: small-caps; font-variant-numeric: oldstyle-nums; text-transform: lowercase;">SG</abbr></p></div><p style="display: none;">oma imitááwa siiksípohsiwa</p><p style="display: none;">om-wa imitáá-wa siiksip-o꞉hsi-wa</p><p style="display: none;">that-AN.SG dog-AN.SG PST:bite(TA)-REFL(AI)-3.SG</p><p style="clear: left;">'That dog bit itself.'</p><div style="clear: left; display: block;"></div>
</div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Relative_clauses">Relative clauses</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Blackfoot_language&amp;action=edit&amp;section=33" title="Edit section: Relative clauses"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Relative clauses are rare in Blackfoot but they do occur. In order to embed a clause, it needs to be nominalized first. The reclassification strategy for nominalization is displayed here followed by a relative clause that uses a nominal formed by this strategy. Reclassification is done by adding nominal inflection to the verb stem instead of person inflection. This derived form then refers to the underlying subject and agrees in both number and animacy.<sup id="cite_ref-46" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-46">&#91;46&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="interlinear" style="margin-left:3em"><div style="float: left; margin-bottom: 0.3em;margin-right: 1em;"><p lang="bla-latn" style="margin: 0px;font-style: italic;">omiksi</p><p style="margin: 0px;">om-iksi</p><p style="margin: 0px;">that-<abbr class="gloss-abbr" title="animate" style="font-variant: small-caps; font-variant-numeric: oldstyle-nums; text-transform: lowercase;">AN</abbr>.<abbr class="gloss-abbr" title="plural number" style="font-variant: small-caps; font-variant-numeric: oldstyle-nums; text-transform: lowercase;">PL</abbr></p></div><div style="float: left; margin-bottom: 0.3em;margin-right: 1em;"><p lang="bla-latn" style="margin: 0px;font-style: italic;">áyoʼkaiksi</p><p style="margin: 0px;">á-yoʼkaa-iksi</p><p style="margin: 0px;"><abbr class="gloss-abbr" title="durative aspect" style="font-variant: small-caps; font-variant-numeric: oldstyle-nums; text-transform: lowercase;">DUR</abbr>-sleep-<abbr class="gloss-abbr" title="animate" style="font-variant: small-caps; font-variant-numeric: oldstyle-nums; text-transform: lowercase;">AN</abbr>.<abbr class="gloss-abbr" title="plural number" style="font-variant: small-caps; font-variant-numeric: oldstyle-nums; text-transform: lowercase;">PL</abbr></p></div><p style="display: none;">omiksi áyoʼkaiksi</p><p style="display: none;">om-iksi á-yoʼkaa-iksi</p><p style="display: none;">that-AN.PL DUR-sleep-AN.PL</p><p style="clear: left;">'those sleeping ones'</p><div style="clear: left; display: block;"></div>
</div>
<p>Examples below show how a reclassified nominalized clause is used in a relative clause. Note the nominal agreement morphology on the verb matches the subject, singular and plural, respectively.
</p>
<div class="interlinear" style="margin-left:3em"><div style="float: left; margin-bottom: 0.3em;margin-right: 1em;"><p lang="bla-latn" style="margin: 0px;font-style: italic;">oma</p><p style="margin: 0px;">om-wa</p><p style="margin: 0px;">that-<abbr class="gloss-abbr" title="animate" style="font-variant: small-caps; font-variant-numeric: oldstyle-nums; text-transform: lowercase;">AN</abbr>.<abbr class="gloss-abbr" title="singular number" style="font-variant: small-caps; font-variant-numeric: oldstyle-nums; text-transform: lowercase;">SG</abbr></p></div><div style="float: left; margin-bottom: 0.3em;margin-right: 1em;"><p lang="bla-latn" style="margin: 0px;font-style: italic;">nínaawa</p><p style="margin: 0px;">ninaa-wa</p><p style="margin: 0px;">man-<abbr class="gloss-abbr" title="animate" style="font-variant: small-caps; font-variant-numeric: oldstyle-nums; text-transform: lowercase;">AN</abbr>.<abbr class="gloss-abbr" title="singular number" style="font-variant: small-caps; font-variant-numeric: oldstyle-nums; text-transform: lowercase;">SG</abbr></p></div><div style="float: left; margin-bottom: 0.3em;margin-right: 1em;"><p lang="bla-latn" style="margin: 0px;font-style: italic;">áyoʼkaawa</p><p style="margin: 0px;">á-yoʼkaa-wa</p><p style="margin: 0px;"><abbr class="gloss-abbr" title="durative aspect" style="font-variant: small-caps; font-variant-numeric: oldstyle-nums; text-transform: lowercase;">DUR</abbr>-sleep-<abbr class="gloss-abbr" title="animate" style="font-variant: small-caps; font-variant-numeric: oldstyle-nums; text-transform: lowercase;">AN</abbr>.<abbr class="gloss-abbr" title="singular number" style="font-variant: small-caps; font-variant-numeric: oldstyle-nums; text-transform: lowercase;">SG</abbr></p></div><div style="float: left; margin-bottom: 0.3em;margin-right: 1em;"><p lang="bla-latn" style="margin: 0px;font-style: italic;">nóoma.</p><p style="margin: 0px;">n-oom-wa</p><p style="margin: 0px;"><abbr class="gloss-abbr" title="first person" style="font-variant: small-caps; font-variant-numeric: oldstyle-nums; text-transform: lowercase;">1</abbr>.<abbr class="gloss-abbr" title="possessive marker" style="font-variant: small-caps; font-variant-numeric: oldstyle-nums; text-transform: lowercase;">POSS</abbr>-husband-<abbr class="gloss-abbr" title="animate" style="font-variant: small-caps; font-variant-numeric: oldstyle-nums; text-transform: lowercase;">AN</abbr>.<abbr class="gloss-abbr" title="singular number" style="font-variant: small-caps; font-variant-numeric: oldstyle-nums; text-transform: lowercase;">SG</abbr></p></div><p style="display: none;">oma nínaawa áyoʼkaawa nóoma.</p><p style="display: none;">om-wa ninaa-wa á-yoʼkaa-wa n-oom-wa</p><p style="display: none;">that-AN.SG man-AN.SG DUR-sleep-AN.SG 1.POSS-husband-AN.SG</p><p style="clear: left;">'That man who is sleeping is my husband.'</p><div style="clear: left; display: block;"></div>
</div>
<div class="interlinear" style="margin-left:3em"><div style="float: left; margin-bottom: 0.3em;margin-right: 1em;"><p lang="bla-latn" style="margin: 0px;font-style: italic;">Omiksi</p><p style="margin: 0px;">om-iks</p><p style="margin: 0px;">that-<abbr class="gloss-abbr" title="animate" style="font-variant: small-caps; font-variant-numeric: oldstyle-nums; text-transform: lowercase;">AN</abbr>.<abbr class="gloss-abbr" title="plural number" style="font-variant: small-caps; font-variant-numeric: oldstyle-nums; text-transform: lowercase;">PL</abbr></p></div><div style="float: left; margin-bottom: 0.3em;margin-right: 1em;"><p lang="bla-latn" style="margin: 0px;font-style: italic;">aakííkoaiksi</p><p style="margin: 0px;">aakííkoaN-iksi</p><p style="margin: 0px;">girl-<abbr class="gloss-abbr" title="animate" style="font-variant: small-caps; font-variant-numeric: oldstyle-nums; text-transform: lowercase;">AN</abbr>.<abbr class="gloss-abbr" title="plural number" style="font-variant: small-caps; font-variant-numeric: oldstyle-nums; text-transform: lowercase;">PL</abbr></p></div><div style="float: left; margin-bottom: 0.3em;margin-right: 1em;"><p lang="bla-latn" style="margin: 0px;font-style: italic;">áínihkiiksi</p><p style="margin: 0px;">á-Inihki-iksi</p><p style="margin: 0px;"><abbr class="gloss-abbr" title="durative aspect" style="font-variant: small-caps; font-variant-numeric: oldstyle-nums; text-transform: lowercase;">DUR</abbr>-sing-<abbr class="gloss-abbr" title="animate" style="font-variant: small-caps; font-variant-numeric: oldstyle-nums; text-transform: lowercase;">AN</abbr>.<abbr class="gloss-abbr" title="plural number" style="font-variant: small-caps; font-variant-numeric: oldstyle-nums; text-transform: lowercase;">PL</abbr></p></div><div style="float: left; margin-bottom: 0.3em;margin-right: 1em;"><p lang="bla-latn" style="margin: 0px;font-style: italic;">áyaakahkayiyaawa.</p><p style="margin: 0px;">áyaak-wa:hkayi-yi-aawa</p><p style="margin: 0px;"><abbr class="gloss-abbr" title="future tense" style="font-variant: small-caps; text-transform: lowercase;">3</abbr>.<abbr class="gloss-abbr" title="plural number" style="font-variant: small-caps; font-variant-numeric: oldstyle-nums; text-transform: lowercase;">PL</abbr>-<abbr class="gloss-abbr" title="pronoun" style="font-variant: small-caps; display: block;"></div>
</div>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Orthography">Orthography<span class="anchor" id="Writing_System"></span></span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Blackfoot_language&amp;action=edit&amp;section=34" title="Edit section: Orthography"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Latin-based_orthography">Latin-based orthography</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Blackfoot_language&amp;action=edit&amp;section=35" title="Edit section: Latin-based orthography"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The Siksiká, Kainai, and Aapátohsipikani reserves adopted a standardized roman-based orthography in 1975. The Blackfoot alphabet consists of 13 letters: <span class="nowrap">&#x27e8;a, h, i, k, m, n, o, p, s, t, w, y&#x27e9;</span>, and a glottal stop (<a href="/wiki/%CA%BC" class="mw-redirect" title="ʼ">ʼ</a>).<sup id="cite_ref-Frantz_2017,_p._163_47-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Frantz_2017,_p._163-47">&#91;47&#93;</a></sup>
</p>

<p>Two digraphs are also used: ts <span class="nowrap">&#x27e8;<span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA" lang="und-Latn-fonipa">ts</span>&#x27e9;</span> and ks <span class="nowrap">&#x27e8;<span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA" lang="und-Latn-fonipa">ks</span>&#x27e9;</span>.
</p>
<table class="IPA wikitable" style="text-align: center">

<tbody><tr>

<p>Vowels can be marked with an acute accent or underlined to illustrate pitch accent. Vowels and consonants that are long are written with a double letter (aa = <span class="nowrap">&#x27e8;<span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA" lang="und-Latn-fonipa">aː</span>&#x27e9;</span>).<sup id="cite_ref-Frantz_2017,_p._163_47-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Frantz_2017,_p._163-47">&#91;47&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Syllabic_writing_system">Syllabic writing system</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Blackfoot_language&amp;action=edit&amp;section=36" title="Edit section: Syllabic writing system"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>A <a href="/wiki/Canadian_Aboriginal_syllabics" title="Canadian Aboriginal syllabics">syllabics</a> script, <span title="Blackfoot-language text"><span lang="bla">ᑯᖾᖹ ᖿᐟᖻ ᓱᖽᐧᖿ</span></span> <span title="Blackfoot-language romanization"><i lang="bla-Latn">pikoni kayna siksika</i></span>, was created by Anglican missionary <a href="/wiki/John_William_Tims" class="mw-redirect" title="John William Tims">John William Tims</a> around 1888, for his Bible translation work. Although conceptually nearly identical to <a href="/wiki/Western_Cree_syllabics" title="Western Cree syllabics">Western Cree syllabics</a>, the letter forms are innovative. Two series (<i>s</i>, <i>y</i>) were taken from Cree but given different vowel values; three more (<i>p</i>, <i>t</i>, <i>m</i>) were changed in consonant values as well, according to the Latin letter they resembled; and the others (<i>k</i>, <i>n</i>, <i>w</i>) were created from asymmetrical parts of Latin and Greek letters; or in the case of the <a href="/wiki/Zero_consonant" title="Zero consonant">zero consonant</a>, possibly from the musical notation for <a href="/wiki/Quarter_note" title="Quarter note">quarter note</a>. The Latin orientation of the letters is used for the <i>e</i> series, after the names of the Latin letters, <i>pe, te,</i> etc.
</p>
<table class="wikitable">
<tbody><tr>
<th>Blackfoot</th>
<th>Latin source
</th></tr>
<tr>
<td>ᑭ <i>pe</i></td>
<td><b>P</b>
</td></tr>
<tr>
<td>ᒥ <i>te</i></td>
<td><b>T</b>
</td></tr>
<tr>
<td>ᖼ <i>ke</i></td>
<td><b>K</b>
</td></tr>
<tr>
<td>ᒋ <i>me</i></td>
<td><b>m</b>
</td></tr>
<tr>
<td>ᖸ <i>ne</i></td>
<td><b>N</b>
</td></tr>
<tr>
<td>ᖴ <i>we</i></td>
<td><a href="/wiki/Digamma" title="Digamma">digamma</a> <b>Ϝ</b>
</td></tr></tbody></table>
<p>The direction for each vowel is different from Cree, reflecting Latin alphabetic order. The <i>e</i> orientation is used for the diphthong <span class="IPA nowrap" lang="und-Latn-fonipa" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/ai/</span>. Symbols for consonants are taken from the consonant symbol minus the stem, except for diphthongs (<i>Ca</i> plus <span class="nowrap">&#x27e8;ᐠ&#x27e9;</span> for <i>Cau</i>, and <i>Ca</i> plus <span class="nowrap">&#x27e8;ᐟ&#x27e9;</span> for <i>Coi</i>, though there are also cases of writing subphonemic <span class="IPA nowrap" lang="und-Latn-fonipa" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">[ai,<span class="wrap"> </span>ei,<span class="wrap"> </span>eu]</span> with these finals).
</p>
